### Overview [¶](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#pkg-overview "Go to Overview")

Package systemconv provides types and functionality for OpenTelemetry semantic conventions in the "system" namespace.

### Index [¶](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#pkg-index "Go to Index")

#### type [CPULogicalCount](https://github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-go/blob/v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv/metric.go#L211)[¶](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#CPULogicalCount "Go to CPULogicalCount")

type CPULogicalCount struct {
[metric](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel/metric).[Int64UpDownCounter](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel/metric#Int64UpDownCounter)}

CPULogicalCount is an instrument used to record metric values conforming to the "system.cpu.logical.count" semantic conventions. It represents the reports the number of logical (virtual) processor cores created by the operating system to manage multitasking.

#### func [NewCPULogicalCount](https://github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-go/blob/v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv/metric.go#L216)[¶](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#NewCPULogicalCount "Go to NewCPULogicalCount")

func NewCPULogicalCount(
	m [metric](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel/metric).[Meter](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel/metric#Meter),
	opt ...[metric](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel/metric).[Int64UpDownCounterOption](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel/metric#Int64UpDownCounterOption),
) ([CPULogicalCount](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#CPULogicalCount), [error](https://pkg.go.dev/builtin#error))

NewCPULogicalCount returns a new CPULogicalCount instrument.

#### func (CPULogicalCount) [Add](https://github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-go/blob/v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv/metric.go#L262)[¶](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#CPULogicalCount.Add "Go to CPULogicalCount.Add")

func (m [CPULogicalCount](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#CPULogicalCount)) Add(ctx [context](https://pkg.go.dev/context).[Context](https://pkg.go.dev/context#Context), incr [int64](https://pkg.go.dev/builtin#int64), attrs ...[attribute](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/attribute).[KeyValue](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/attribute#KeyValue))

Add adds incr to the existing count.

Calculated by multiplying the number of sockets by the number of cores per socket, and then by the number of threads per core

#### type [CPUPhysicalCount](https://github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-go/blob/v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv/metric.go#L281)[¶](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#CPUPhysicalCount "Go to CPUPhysicalCount")

type CPUPhysicalCount struct {
[metric](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel/metric).[Int64UpDownCounter](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel/metric#Int64UpDownCounter)}

CPUPhysicalCount is an instrument used to record metric values conforming to the "system.cpu.physical.count" semantic conventions. It represents the reports the number of actual physical processor cores on the hardware.

#### func [NewCPUPhysicalCount](https://github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-go/blob/v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv/metric.go#L286)[¶](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#NewCPUPhysicalCount "Go to NewCPUPhysicalCount")

	opt ...[metric](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel/metric).[Int64UpDownCounterOption](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel/metric#Int64UpDownCounterOption),

Calculated by multiplying the number of sockets by the number of cores per socket

#### func (CPUPhysicalCount) [Description](https://github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-go/blob/v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv/metric.go#L324)[¶](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#CPUPhysicalCount.Description "Go to CPUPhysicalCount.Description")

// DiskIODirectionRead is the none.	DiskIODirectionRead [DiskIODirectionAttr](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#DiskIODirectionAttr) = "read"
// DiskIODirectionWrite is the none.	DiskIODirectionWrite [DiskIODirectionAttr](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#DiskIODirectionAttr) = "write"

#### type [DiskIOTime](https://github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-go/blob/v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv/metric.go#L431)[¶](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#DiskIOTime "Go to DiskIOTime")

type DiskIOTime struct {
[metric](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel/metric).[Float64Counter](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel/metric#Float64Counter)}

DiskIOTime is an instrument used to record metric values conforming to the "system.disk.io_time" semantic conventions. It represents the time disk spent activated.

#### func [NewDiskIOTime](https://github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-go/blob/v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv/metric.go#L436)[¶](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#NewDiskIOTime "Go to NewDiskIOTime")

func NewDiskIOTime(
	m [metric](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel/metric).[Meter](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel/metric#Meter),
	opt ...[metric](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel/metric).[Float64CounterOption](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel/metric#Float64CounterOption),
) ([DiskIOTime](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#DiskIOTime), [error](https://pkg.go.dev/builtin#error))

NewDiskIOTime returns a new DiskIOTime instrument.

#### func (DiskIOTime) [Add](https://github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-go/blob/v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv/metric.go#L493)[¶](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#DiskIOTime.Add "Go to DiskIOTime.Add")

func (m [DiskIOTime](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#DiskIOTime)) Add(
	ctx [context](https://pkg.go.dev/context).[Context](https://pkg.go.dev/context#Context),
	incr [float64](https://pkg.go.dev/builtin#float64),
	attrs ...[attribute](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/attribute).[KeyValue](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/attribute#KeyValue),
)

Add adds incr to the existing count.

All additional attrs passed are included in the recorded value.

The real elapsed time ("wall clock") used in the I/O path (time from operations running in parallel are not counted). Measured as:

*   Linux: Field 13 from [procfs-diskstats](https://www.kernel.org/doc/Documentation/ABI/testing/procfs-diskstats)
*   Windows: The complement of ["Disk% Idle Time"](https://learn.microsoft.com/archive/blogs/askcore/windows-performance-monitor-disk-counters-explained#windows-performance-monitor-disk-counters-explained) performance counter: `uptime * (100 - "Disk\% Idle Time") / 100`

#### type [DiskOperationTime](https://github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-go/blob/v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv/metric.go#L683)[¶](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#DiskOperationTime "Go to DiskOperationTime")

type DiskOperationTime struct {
[metric](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel/metric).[Float64Counter](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel/metric#Float64Counter)}

DiskOperationTime is an instrument used to record metric values conforming to the "system.disk.operation_time" semantic conventions. It represents the sum of the time each operation took to complete.

#### func [NewDiskOperationTime](https://github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-go/blob/v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv/metric.go#L688)[¶](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#NewDiskOperationTime "Go to NewDiskOperationTime")

func NewDiskOperationTime(
	m [metric](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel/metric).[Meter](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel/metric#Meter),
	opt ...[metric](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel/metric).[Float64CounterOption](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel/metric#Float64CounterOption),
) ([DiskOperationTime](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#DiskOperationTime), [error](https://pkg.go.dev/builtin#error))

NewDiskOperationTime returns a new DiskOperationTime instrument.

#### func (DiskOperationTime) [Add](https://github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-go/blob/v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv/metric.go#L743)[¶](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#DiskOperationTime.Add "Go to DiskOperationTime.Add")

func (m [DiskOperationTime](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#DiskOperationTime)) Add(
	ctx [context](https://pkg.go.dev/context).[Context](https://pkg.go.dev/context#Context),
	incr [float64](https://pkg.go.dev/builtin#float64),
	attrs ...[attribute](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/attribute).[KeyValue](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/attribute#KeyValue),
)

Add adds incr to the existing count.

All additional attrs passed are included in the recorded value.

Because it is the sum of time each request took, parallel-issued requests each contribute to make the count grow. Measured as:

*   Linux: Fields 7 & 11 from [procfs-diskstats](https://www.kernel.org/doc/Documentation/ABI/testing/procfs-diskstats)
*   Windows: "Avg. Disk sec/Read" perf counter multiplied by "Disk Reads/sec" perf counter (similar for Writes)

#### type [FilesystemUsage](https://github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-go/blob/v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv/metric.go#L961)[¶](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#FilesystemUsage "Go to FilesystemUsage")

type FilesystemUsage struct {
[metric](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel/metric).[Int64UpDownCounter](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel/metric#Int64UpDownCounter)}

FilesystemUsage is an instrument used to record metric values conforming to the "system.filesystem.usage" semantic conventions. It represents the reports a filesystem's space usage across different states.

#### func [NewFilesystemUsage](https://github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-go/blob/v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv/metric.go#L966)[¶](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#NewFilesystemUsage "Go to NewFilesystemUsage")

func NewFilesystemUsage(
	m [metric](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel/metric).[Meter](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel/metric#Meter),
	opt ...[metric](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel/metric).[Int64UpDownCounterOption](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel/metric#Int64UpDownCounterOption),
) ([FilesystemUsage](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#FilesystemUsage), [error](https://pkg.go.dev/builtin#error))

NewFilesystemUsage returns a new FilesystemUsage instrument.

#### func (FilesystemUsage) [Add](https://github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-go/blob/v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv/metric.go#L1016)[¶](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#FilesystemUsage.Add "Go to FilesystemUsage.Add")

func (m [FilesystemUsage](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#FilesystemUsage)) Add(
	ctx [context](https://pkg.go.dev/context).[Context](https://pkg.go.dev/context#Context),
	incr [int64](https://pkg.go.dev/builtin#int64),
	attrs ...[attribute](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/attribute).[KeyValue](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/attribute#KeyValue),
)

Add adds incr to the existing count.

All additional attrs passed are included in the recorded value.

The sum of all `system.filesystem.usage` values over the different `system.filesystem.state` attributes SHOULD equal the total storage capacity of the filesystem, that is `system.filesystem.limit`.

#### type [LinuxMemoryAvailable](https://github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-go/blob/v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv/metric.go#L1179)[¶](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#LinuxMemoryAvailable "Go to LinuxMemoryAvailable")

type LinuxMemoryAvailable struct {
[metric](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel/metric).[Int64UpDownCounter](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel/metric#Int64UpDownCounter)}

LinuxMemoryAvailable is an instrument used to record metric values conforming to the "system.linux.memory.available" semantic conventions. It represents an estimate of how much memory is available for starting new applications, without causing swapping.

#### func [NewLinuxMemoryAvailable](https://github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-go/blob/v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv/metric.go#L1184)[¶](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#NewLinuxMemoryAvailable "Go to NewLinuxMemoryAvailable")

func NewLinuxMemoryAvailable(
	m [metric](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel/metric).[Meter](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel/metric#Meter),
	opt ...[metric](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel/metric).[Int64UpDownCounterOption](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel/metric#Int64UpDownCounterOption),
) ([LinuxMemoryAvailable](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#LinuxMemoryAvailable), [error](https://pkg.go.dev/builtin#error))

NewLinuxMemoryAvailable returns a new LinuxMemoryAvailable instrument.

#### func (LinuxMemoryAvailable) [Add](https://github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-go/blob/v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv/metric.go#L1237)[¶](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#LinuxMemoryAvailable.Add "Go to LinuxMemoryAvailable.Add")

func (m [LinuxMemoryAvailable](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#LinuxMemoryAvailable)) Add(ctx [context](https://pkg.go.dev/context).[Context](https://pkg.go.dev/context#Context), incr [int64](https://pkg.go.dev/builtin#int64), attrs ...[attribute](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/attribute).[KeyValue](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/attribute#KeyValue))

Add adds incr to the existing count.

This is an alternative to `system.memory.usage` metric with `state=free`. Linux starting from 3.14 exports "available" memory. It takes "free" memory as a baseline, and then factors in kernel-specific values. This is supposed to be more accurate than just "free" memory. For reference, see the calculations [here](https://superuser.com/a/980821). See also `MemAvailable` in [/proc/meminfo](https://man7.org/linux/man-pages/man5/proc.5.html).

#### func (LinuxMemoryAvailable) [Description](https://github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-go/blob/v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv/metric.go#L1222)[¶](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#LinuxMemoryAvailable.Description "Go to LinuxMemoryAvailable.Description")

#### type [LinuxMemorySlabStateAttr](https://github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-go/blob/v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv/metric.go#L38)[¶](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#LinuxMemorySlabStateAttr "Go to LinuxMemorySlabStateAttr")

type LinuxMemorySlabStateAttr [string](https://pkg.go.dev/builtin#string)

LinuxMemorySlabStateAttr is an attribute conforming to the linux.memory.slab.state semantic conventions. It represents the Linux Slab memory state.

var (
// LinuxMemorySlabStateReclaimable is the none.	LinuxMemorySlabStateReclaimable [LinuxMemorySlabStateAttr](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#LinuxMemorySlabStateAttr) = "reclaimable"
// LinuxMemorySlabStateUnreclaimable is the none.	LinuxMemorySlabStateUnreclaimable [LinuxMemorySlabStateAttr](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#LinuxMemorySlabStateAttr) = "unreclaimable"
)

#### type [LinuxMemorySlabUsage](https://github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-go/blob/v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv/metric.go#L1257)[¶](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#LinuxMemorySlabUsage "Go to LinuxMemorySlabUsage")

type LinuxMemorySlabUsage struct {
[metric](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel/metric).[Int64UpDownCounter](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel/metric#Int64UpDownCounter)}

LinuxMemorySlabUsage is an instrument used to record metric values conforming to the "system.linux.memory.slab.usage" semantic conventions. It represents the reports the memory used by the Linux kernel for managing caches of frequently used objects.

#### func [NewLinuxMemorySlabUsage](https://github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-go/blob/v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv/metric.go#L1262)[¶](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#NewLinuxMemorySlabUsage "Go to NewLinuxMemorySlabUsage")

func NewLinuxMemorySlabUsage(
	m [metric](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel/metric).[Meter](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel/metric#Meter),
	opt ...[metric](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel/metric).[Int64UpDownCounterOption](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel/metric#Int64UpDownCounterOption),
) ([LinuxMemorySlabUsage](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#LinuxMemorySlabUsage), [error](https://pkg.go.dev/builtin#error))

NewLinuxMemorySlabUsage returns a new LinuxMemorySlabUsage instrument.

#### func (LinuxMemorySlabUsage) [Add](https://github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-go/blob/v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv/metric.go#L1316)[¶](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#LinuxMemorySlabUsage.Add "Go to LinuxMemorySlabUsage.Add")

func (m [LinuxMemorySlabUsage](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#LinuxMemorySlabUsage)) Add(
	ctx [context](https://pkg.go.dev/context).[Context](https://pkg.go.dev/context#Context),
	incr [int64](https://pkg.go.dev/builtin#int64),
	attrs ...[attribute](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/attribute).[KeyValue](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/attribute#KeyValue),
)

Add adds incr to the existing count.

All additional attrs passed are included in the recorded value.

The sum over the `reclaimable` and `unreclaimable` state values in `linux.memory.slab.usage` SHOULD be equal to the total slab memory available on the system. Note that the total slab memory is not constant and may vary over time. See also the [Slab allocator](https://blogs.oracle.com/linux/post/understanding-linux-kernel-memory-statistics) and `Slab` in [/proc/meminfo](https://man7.org/linux/man-pages/man5/proc.5.html).

#### func (LinuxMemorySlabUsage) [AttrLinuxMemorySlabState](https://github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-go/blob/v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv/metric.go#L1340)[¶](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#LinuxMemorySlabUsage.AttrLinuxMemorySlabState "Go to LinuxMemorySlabUsage.AttrLinuxMemorySlabState")

AttrLinuxMemorySlabState returns an optional attribute for the "linux.memory.slab.state" semantic convention. It represents the Linux Slab memory state.

#### type [MemoryLimit](https://github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-go/blob/v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv/metric.go#L1347)[¶](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#MemoryLimit "Go to MemoryLimit")

type MemoryLimit struct {
[metric](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel/metric).[Int64UpDownCounter](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel/metric#Int64UpDownCounter)}

MemoryLimit is an instrument used to record metric values conforming to the "system.memory.limit" semantic conventions. It represents the total memory available in the system.

#### func (MemoryLimit) [Add](https://github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-go/blob/v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv/metric.go#L1397)[¶](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#MemoryLimit.Add "Go to MemoryLimit.Add")

func (m [MemoryLimit](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#MemoryLimit)) Add(ctx [context](https://pkg.go.dev/context).[Context](https://pkg.go.dev/context#Context), incr [int64](https://pkg.go.dev/builtin#int64), attrs ...[attribute](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/attribute).[KeyValue](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/attribute#KeyValue))

Add adds incr to the existing count.

Its value SHOULD equal the sum of `system.memory.state` over all states.

#### type [MemoryShared](https://github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-go/blob/v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv/metric.go#L1416)[¶](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#MemoryShared "Go to MemoryShared")

type MemoryShared struct {
[metric](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel/metric).[Int64UpDownCounter](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel/metric#Int64UpDownCounter)}

MemoryShared is an instrument used to record metric values conforming to the "system.memory.shared" semantic conventions. It represents the shared memory used (mostly by tmpfs).

#### type [MemoryStateAttr](https://github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-go/blob/v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv/metric.go#L143)[¶](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#MemoryStateAttr "Go to MemoryStateAttr")

type MemoryStateAttr [string](https://pkg.go.dev/builtin#string)

MemoryStateAttr is an attribute conforming to the system.memory.state semantic conventions. It represents the memory state.

var (
// MemoryStateUsed is the none.	MemoryStateUsed [MemoryStateAttr](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#MemoryStateAttr) = "used"
// MemoryStateFree is the none.	MemoryStateFree [MemoryStateAttr](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#MemoryStateAttr) = "free"
// MemoryStateBuffers is the none.	MemoryStateBuffers [MemoryStateAttr](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#MemoryStateAttr) = "buffers"

#### type [NetworkDropped](https://github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-go/blob/v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv/metric.go#L1687)[¶](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#NetworkDropped "Go to NetworkDropped")

type NetworkDropped struct {
[metric](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel/metric).[Int64Counter](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel/metric#Int64Counter)}

NetworkDropped is an instrument used to record metric values conforming to the "system.network.dropped" semantic conventions. It represents the count of packets that are dropped or discarded even though there was no error.

#### func [NewNetworkDropped](https://github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-go/blob/v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv/metric.go#L1692)[¶](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#NewNetworkDropped "Go to NewNetworkDropped")

	m [metric](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel/metric).[Meter](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel/metric#Meter),
	opt ...[metric](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel/metric).[Int64CounterOption](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel/metric#Int64CounterOption),
) ([NetworkDropped](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#NetworkDropped), [error](https://pkg.go.dev/builtin#error))

NewNetworkDropped returns a new NetworkDropped instrument.

#### func (NetworkDropped) [Add](https://github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-go/blob/v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv/metric.go#L1748)[¶](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#NetworkDropped.Add "Go to NetworkDropped.Add")

func (m [NetworkDropped](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#NetworkDropped)) Add(
	ctx [context](https://pkg.go.dev/context).[Context](https://pkg.go.dev/context#Context),
	incr [int64](https://pkg.go.dev/builtin#int64),
	attrs ...[attribute](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/attribute).[KeyValue](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/attribute#KeyValue),
)

Add adds incr to the existing count.

All additional attrs passed are included in the recorded value.

Measured as:

*   Linux: the `drop` column in `/proc/dev/net` ([source](https://web.archive.org/web/20180321091318/http://www.onlamp.com/pub/a/linux/2000/11/16/LinuxAdmin.html))
*   Windows: [`InDiscards`/`OutDiscards`](https://docs.microsoft.com/windows/win32/api/netioapi/ns-netioapi-mib_if_row2) from [`GetIfEntry2`](https://docs.microsoft.com/windows/win32/api/netioapi/nf-netioapi-getifentry2)

#### type [NetworkErrors](https://github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-go/blob/v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv/metric.go#L1786)[¶](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#NetworkErrors "Go to NetworkErrors")

type NetworkErrors struct {
[metric](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel/metric).[Int64Counter](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel/metric#Int64Counter)}

NetworkErrors is an instrument used to record metric values conforming to the "system.network.errors" semantic conventions. It represents the count of network errors detected.

#### func [NewNetworkErrors](https://github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-go/blob/v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv/metric.go#L1791)[¶](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#NewNetworkErrors "Go to NewNetworkErrors")

	opt ...[metric](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel/metric).[Int64CounterOption](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel/metric#Int64CounterOption),
) ([NetworkErrors](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#NetworkErrors), [error](https://pkg.go.dev/builtin#error))

NewNetworkErrors returns a new NetworkErrors instrument.

#### func (NetworkErrors) [Add](https://github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-go/blob/v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv/metric.go#L1847)[¶](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#NetworkErrors.Add "Go to NetworkErrors.Add")

func (m [NetworkErrors](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#NetworkErrors)) Add(
	ctx [context](https://pkg.go.dev/context).[Context](https://pkg.go.dev/context#Context),
	incr [int64](https://pkg.go.dev/builtin#int64),
	attrs ...[attribute](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/attribute).[KeyValue](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/attribute#KeyValue),
)

Add adds incr to the existing count.

All additional attrs passed are included in the recorded value.

Measured as:

*   Linux: the `errs` column in `/proc/dev/net` ([source](https://web.archive.org/web/20180321091318/http://www.onlamp.com/pub/a/linux/2000/11/16/LinuxAdmin.html)).
*   Windows: [`InErrors`/`OutErrors`](https://docs.microsoft.com/windows/win32/api/netioapi/ns-netioapi-mib_if_row2) from [`GetIfEntry2`](https://docs.microsoft.com/windows/win32/api/netioapi/nf-netioapi-getifentry2).

)

#### type [NetworkTransportAttr](https://github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-go/blob/v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv/metric.go#L94)[¶](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#NetworkTransportAttr "Go to NetworkTransportAttr")

type NetworkTransportAttr [string](https://pkg.go.dev/builtin#string)

NetworkTransportAttr is an attribute conforming to the network.transport semantic conventions. It represents the [OSI transport layer](https://wikipedia.org/wiki/Transport_layer) or [inter-process communication method](https://wikipedia.org/wiki/Inter-process_communication).

var (
// NetworkTransportTCP is the TCP.	NetworkTransportTCP [NetworkTransportAttr](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#NetworkTransportAttr) = "tcp"
// NetworkTransportUDP is the UDP.	NetworkTransportUDP [NetworkTransportAttr](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#NetworkTransportAttr) = "udp"
// NetworkTransportPipe is the named or anonymous pipe.	NetworkTransportPipe [NetworkTransportAttr](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#NetworkTransportAttr) = "pipe"
// NetworkTransportUnix is the unix domain socket.	NetworkTransportUnix [NetworkTransportAttr](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#NetworkTransportAttr) = "unix"
// NetworkTransportQUIC is the QUIC.	NetworkTransportQUIC [NetworkTransportAttr](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#NetworkTransportAttr) = "quic"
)

#### type [ProcessStatusAttr](https://github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-go/blob/v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv/metric.go#L194)[¶](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#ProcessStatusAttr "Go to ProcessStatusAttr")

type ProcessStatusAttr [string](https://pkg.go.dev/builtin#string)

ProcessStatusAttr is an attribute conforming to the system.process.status semantic conventions. It represents the process state, e.g., [Linux Process State Codes](https://man7.org/linux/man-pages/man1/ps.1.html#PROCESS_STATE_CODES).

var (
// ProcessStatusRunning is the none.	ProcessStatusRunning [ProcessStatusAttr](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#ProcessStatusAttr) = "running"
// ProcessStatusSleeping is the none.	ProcessStatusSleeping [ProcessStatusAttr](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#ProcessStatusAttr) = "sleeping"
// ProcessStatusStopped is the none.	ProcessStatusStopped [ProcessStatusAttr](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#ProcessStatusAttr) = "stopped"
// ProcessStatusDefunct is the none.	ProcessStatusDefunct [ProcessStatusAttr](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#ProcessStatusAttr) = "defunct"
)

#### type [Uptime](https://github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-go/blob/v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv/metric.go#L2497)[¶](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#Uptime "Go to Uptime")

Uptime is an instrument used to record metric values conforming to the "system.uptime" semantic conventions. It represents the time the system has been running.

#### func (Uptime) [Record](https://github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-go/blob/v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv/metric.go#L2549)[¶](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#Uptime.Record "Go to Uptime.Record")

func (m [Uptime](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#Uptime)) Record(ctx [context](https://pkg.go.dev/context).[Context](https://pkg.go.dev/context#Context), val [float64](https://pkg.go.dev/builtin#float64), attrs ...[attribute](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/attribute).[KeyValue](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/attribute#KeyValue))

Record records val to the current distribution.

Instrumentations SHOULD use a gauge with type `double` and measure uptime in seconds as a floating point number with the highest precision available. The actual accuracy would depend on the instrumentation and operating system.

#### func (Uptime) [Unit](https://github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-go/blob/v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv/metric.go#L2535)[¶](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel@v1.40.0/semconv/v1.33.0/systemconv#Uptime.Unit "Go to Uptime.Unit")
